The game and its variants are popular in many countries and under various names.\r\n\r\nParchisi originated in India by the 6th century. \r\n\r\nEach player rolls the die; the highest roller begins the game. The checkers are always moved forward. The following rules apply:\r\n- The numbers on the two dice constitute separate moves. For example, if a player rolls 5 and 3, he may move one checker five spaces to an open point and another (or same) checker three spaces to an open point.\r\n- A player who rolls doubles plays the numbers shown on the dice twice. A roll of 6 and 6 means that the player has four sixes to use.\r\n- A player must use both (or all 4 for doubles) numbers of a roll if this is legally possible. Or if either number can be played but not both, the player must play the larger one.\r\n- Once a player has moved all of his fifteen checkers into his home board, he may commence bearing off.
